  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_704df43d-646f-4668-a524-83bb8459e4c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText13101262104781392139" style="display:none">Carly Adams feels as if she's been given a new lease on life. Born with a rare eye disease, she was blind until a recent operation restored her sight. Now, she's eager to experience everything the world has to offer—including the sweet talk of a handsome cowboy who rouses her with desire. But she isn't prepared for the consequences, especially when a night of searing passion results in a pregnancy that threatens her eyesight—and all her dreams for the future . . . .<br /><br />Hank Coulter has no plans to settle down—until he discovers that Carly Adams is carrying his child. Obsessed with making things right, he bullies the blue-eyed beauty into marrying him. With her radiant smile and remarkable goodness, Carly is exactly the kind of wife he's always imagined by his side. But if Hank wants their practical arrangement to become permanent, he's going to have to convince Carly that one moment of risk can bring about a lifetime of joy . . . .</span>

<div id="review_1235205" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1235205" />
    <a title="Rhapsody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21602-rhapsody"><img alt="Rhapsody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1179613973p2/21602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1235205?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhapsody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhapsody" href="/user/show/21602-rhapsody">Rhapsody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like beating-the-odds love stories</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21602-rhapsody?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21602-rhapsody?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1235205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5628233775381048254">This book irked me a little. I didn't like the way a lot of the characters behaved, and when they started behaving better, it got a little too sappy for me. Carly, the heroine, just had surgery that's given her vision after being blind all her life. Two weeks after the surgery, she goes to a bar and gets knocked up by Hank Coulter. She was told that getting pregnant right after the surgery would be very bad and now she's going to go blind again, can't afford to take care of the baby on the way, </span>
  <span id="freeText5628233775381048254" style="display:none">This book irked me a little. I didn't like the way a lot of the characters behaved, and when they started behaving better, it got a little too sappy for me. Carly, the heroine, just had surgery that's given her vision after being blind all her life. Two weeks after the surgery, she goes to a bar and gets knocked up by Hank Coulter. She was told that getting pregnant right after the surgery would be very bad and now she's going to go blind again, can't afford to take care of the baby on the way, and her plans to go to grad school are ruined. Hank offers to marry her, she accepts, they slowly fall in love, blablabla...<br /><br />Everyone was so irresponsible in this book, Carly most of all, but she's portrayed mainly as a victim/martyr. It really annoys me that knowing she wasn't supposed to get pregnant, she still went to that cowboy bar and then had sex with a total stranger in the back of a truck. I don't care how vulnerable she was, it was stupid. Then when she realizes she's pregnant, she won't even consider abortion. Okay, it's a sensitive topic, but not only did she have no way of supporting a child, it was going to ruin her future. When an opportunity to salvage her future and take care of her kid half-presents itself in Hank trying to help, she pushes him away again and again until he finally has to blackmail her. I just can't stand Carly. In addition, most of the book is spent with everyone blaming Hank for getting her pregnant. She does eventually admit to bearing some of the blame, but it comes so late I can't give her much credit for it. For a character who's soooooo "strong-willed" and "independent" and all, it took her long enough to realize she had a little personal accountability for the situation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5628233775381048254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Becky " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30272643-becky"><img alt="Becky " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414176610p2/30272643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130388251?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky " href="/user/show/30272643-becky">Becky </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130388251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1022613762304322103">Wow....what a beautiful story. Hank is a 32 year old rancher who trolls a country western bar every weekend looking for the next one-night stand. He feeds women lines, uses them and then and disappears the next morning. His pick-up one drunken night is Carly, a 28 year old virgin who had a recent operation leading to temporary sightedness. Major consequences of his callous, deceitful approach result. I really enjoyed his growth, but major slut shaming during the book (virgins don't deserve such </span>
  <span id="freeText1022613762304322103" style="display:none">Wow....what a beautiful story. Hank is a 32 year old rancher who trolls a country western bar every weekend looking for the next one-night stand. He feeds women lines, uses them and then and disappears the next morning. His pick-up one drunken night is Carly, a 28 year old virgin who had a recent operation leading to temporary sightedness. Major consequences of his callous, deceitful approach result. I really enjoyed his growth, but major slut shaming during the book (virgins don't deserve such treatment but all other women are just "run of the mill" barfly types that have been "rode hard and put up wet" so are beneath him. After he sleeps with them, of course. And his dad "tossed a number of skirts" before meeting a "good" girl.). But then hero really does see how wrong he was and actually realizes that treating any woman that way was just wrong and diminished him. <br /><br />Very believable transformation and beautiful story about love (as action, not just words), honor, sacrifice, redemption and commitment. It's about those things in the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15931.The_Notebook__The_Notebook___1_" title="The Notebook (The Notebook, #1) by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Notebook</a> ultimately is. And so beautifully written. How could it have been so heartfelt, poetic and heartwarming without being treacly? It just was....that's the author's talent.<br /><br />Loved the secondary characters, Carly's friend Bess, her dad (in the most poignant scene in the book) and Luke's family. I kept hearing his mom as the voice of Marion Cunningham from Happy Days! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1022613762304322103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3982627201070399352">Overall rating: 4.5 stars!<br/><br/>Triggers:<br/>Cheating: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ No. There are no other women at all in this book.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/>Love triangle: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ No  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/>Sex with om/ow: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ No <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ After being the responsible one in his family for much of his young childhood through college, Hank recently (within the last year) has started to frequent bars on the weekends and most of the time he would hook up with a willing female. SO you could say he was a bit of a</span></span></span>
  <span id="freeText3982627201070399352" style="display:none">Overall rating: 4.5 stars!<br /><br />Triggers:<br />Cheating: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ No. There are no other women at all in this book.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ No  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Sex with om/ow: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ No <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ After being the responsible one in his family for much of his young childhood through college, Hank recently (within the last year) has started to frequent bars on the weekends and most of the time he would hook up with a willing female. SO you could say he was a bit of a man ho for awhile there. Once he sleeps with the heroine, because of the circumstances (not because he was in instant love with the heroine) he changes his ways. There is no sex with the hero and other women after he is intimate with the heroine,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />HEA: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ yes  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My review:<br /><br />I was really worried about reading this book at first because of the hero being a bit of a man ho in the beginning of the book, but it really was a non-issue. THANKS BECKY! <br /><br />Basically, Carly has this rare eye disorder (lattice dystrophy) that has caused her to be blind from birth. At the start of this story, she has just undergone a surgery that will finally allow her to see. During this time she is taking in as much as she can because there is no guarantee how long her sight will last and she has missed out on so much already. So one night, about a week in a half after her surgery, she goes out to a local bar with his best friend. She just wants to see people dancing! Something she has never seen before. This is where Hank comes in.<br /><br />Hank has always had to be the responsible one in his family - from high school through college and even at the start of his career. Over this last year, he FINALLY has the chance to play around (at 32 years old) and just have fun with no strings. He frequents this one bar every weekend in order to have some drinks, some dancing and hopefully hook up with a willing female. Then he spots Carly. Even though Hank was three sheets to the wind, she literally takes his breathe away. Of course, he wasn't in love with her at first sight or anything, he actually does charm her like he would any other girl that night that he was looking to score with. Carly, though, is not used to this attention and even though she feels like he HAS to be bullshitting her, also wants to just let loose and see where things go. <br /><br />What I DID appreciate about this book was the hero's attitude. I felt like he wasn't like some heroes who are manwhores turned celibate for love in that he wasn't disrespectful at all towards women. Meaning, he didn't call the women he slept with previously "sluts" or anything like that. And instead of putting the blame on these "sluts" like some heroes will do, he puts the blame on himself for his lifestyle and the way he was living. He understands what being reckless can do. And for Carly, it doesn't just change her life to become a mother, it also causes major problems with his eye disease.<br /><br />It is the result and aftermath of this night that sets the pace for the book. I won't give any more information because I feel like it will totally spoil the story. Why not 5 stars? Well, the heroine REALLY bothered me at some parts. I feel like she gave Hank a really really hard time for majority of the book. Don't get me wrong, I am glad she didn't make it easy on him, but at the same time, he was so damn perfect, I wished she would have caved a little sooner. Also, I wished that the story went more into the future for these two characters. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this book and will definitely recommend it to others!<br /><br />Favorite Quotes: <br /><br /><b> "Sweet," Hank whispered. "So sweet that I need to be horsewhipped for ever touching her." </b><br /><br /><br /><b> "I enjoy hanging up on you. It gives me a perverse satisfaction." <br />Brief silence. There was another smile in his voice when he said, "I always like to satisfy a lady. Go for broke."<br />Carly grinned in spit of herself as she dropped the receiver into the cradle without telling him goodbye. </b><br /><br /><br /><b> He slipped an arm under her shoulders and drew her against him. "Come with me," he whispered. "I'll take you to paradise." </b><br /><br /><br /><b> "Sunlight has never touched anything so beautiful as you. <i> Nothing </i>." </b><br /><br /><br /><b> When she reached his wrists, he turned his hands palm up and ended the kiss to grab for breath. "These hands will always be there," he whispered. "Your strength when your own is flagging, your support when you can't stand alone. I meant this vows when I said them. I stand behind them now, and I'll still do my damnedest to honor them when I'm an old man. There's just one more vow I'd like to make." <br />"What's that?" she asked.<br />"That my eyes are yours as well. When you go blind, I'll draw pictures with words so you can still see all the beautiful things. You told me once that the most gorgeous thing you first saw was the Central Oregon blue sky. That's my vow to you, Carly-nothing but blue skies for the rest of our live, even after you go permanently blind." </b></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/925549-miss-kim?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25937349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8965226916151361013">Ok, I couldn't spare more than 3 stars for this one. I was about one third through Blue Sky and the story line was SO irritating me. The heroine, Carley, has an eye disease that has caused her to blind since birth. After college, she has a surgery that restores a good percent of sight. She has been able to see for about 3 weeks when she goes to the bar with her friend, and proceeds to get hammered, then she sleeps with a stranger in the back of his truck. I forgot to throw in that she was a virg</span>
  <span id="freeText8965226916151361013" style="display:none">Ok, I couldn't spare more than 3 stars for this one. I was about one third through Blue Sky and the story line was SO irritating me. The heroine, Carley, has an eye disease that has caused her to blind since birth. After college, she has a surgery that restores a good percent of sight. She has been able to see for about 3 weeks when she goes to the bar with her friend, and proceeds to get hammered, then she sleeps with a stranger in the back of his truck. I forgot to throw in that she was a virgin, too. Guess what's next? She ends up pregnant. Her surgeons advise her that with her disease, that getting pregnant is a bad idea because it wall cause her to go blind again. Carley comes off as a an angry shrew, and is always crying or yelling through the entire story. Hank, the hero, is a wonderful guy who feels awful about their one night stand afterward. Then she informs him of the pregnancy and wants to marry here to help her with medical expenses, etc. and to also participate in the baby's life. She is reluctant to trust him and she treats him like crap for most of the book. I just can't believe he'd stick with this woman when he gets hardly anything in return. Way late in the book she does start to redeem herself to me, but I still think she is angry selfish brat, and Hank shouldn't have to try so hard to please her. I really liked all the prior books in this series, and was disappointed in this one. However, they do have a nice HEA, and it was not an awful story.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296710618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7790205212038719046">This book is very stereo typical. As a blind person, I don't think I need special ropes and things to get around the ranch independently. I would do just fine on my own. Also, if I could see for the first time, one of the first things I would not do is go to a bar. Oh, and as far as the hunky cowboy, give me a break! Granted, Carly is a grown woman, but, someone has kept her sheltered quite a bit. If she doesn't know the ins and outs of men or the birds and the bees, at least a little bit by now</span>
  <span id="freeText7790205212038719046" style="display:none">This book is very stereo typical. As a blind person, I don't think I need special ropes and things to get around the ranch independently. I would do just fine on my own. Also, if I could see for the first time, one of the first things I would not do is go to a bar. Oh, and as far as the hunky cowboy, give me a break! Granted, Carly is a grown woman, but, someone has kept her sheltered quite a bit. If she doesn't know the ins and outs of men or the birds and the bees, at least a little bit by now, she sorely lacking. People who've never been around blind people, or just do a little bit of research, probably shouldn't write books about them. It's kind of insulting. For those who don't know, most of us do quite well on her own. For us, blindness is simply a nuisance, not a character flaw, and most of us don't run around expecting others to do for us, and pave the way. If I happened to get pregnant even by accident, I wouldn't let the man to marry me because he felt sorry for me and that's exactly what happened in this book. Maybe they did fall in love afterwards, maybe not, but the fact remains, in the beginning, he felt sorry, and tried to do the right thing. Guess what, it didn't work.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13190274712290936367">I really like this book! So far every book in the series has been EXCELLENT! Anderson's stories are always so tender and sweet. I love her less than perfect heroines who find their prince charming in the hunky cowboys who’d move heaven and earth for them! <br/><br/>I was so drawn into the story at page one. Carly was blind all her life but recently went through surgery to regain her sight so when she first sees Hank Coulter at a local bar she thinks he’s the most gorgeous man she’s ever seen.   <span id="freeText13190274712290936367" style="display:none">I really like this book! So far every book in the series has been EXCELLENT! Anderson's stories are always so tender and sweet. I love her less than perfect heroines who find their prince charming in the hunky cowboys who’d move heaven and earth for them! <br /><br />I was so drawn into the story at page one. Carly was blind all her life but recently went through surgery to regain her sight so when she first sees Hank Coulter at a local bar she thinks he’s the most gorgeous man she’s ever seen. When he walks straight to her, dances with her and calls her the most beautiful girl in the bar Carly gets caught up in the moment. For the first time in her life the hottest guy has eyes only for her. Who cares if he’s feeding her lines to get her in bed? She’s been blind all her life so she decides to go with it. Both completely wasted, they get hot and heavy and end up in the back seat of Hank’s truck. When Hank realizes Carly was a virgin he swears under his tongue and passes out! The next morning Hank wakes up in his truck with hangover and can’t believe what he’s done! <br /><br />Weeks later Carly is pregnant but the pregnancy will have a negative effect on her sight and eventually she will lose her sight again completely. There is no way Carly can finish school, hold a job and care for a baby if she’s blind. She does not want to have anything to do with Hank Coulter because he made an absolute fool of her but she has no other choice. She has to contact him. Hank steps up to his responsibilities and he won’t have his child growing up without a father. They get married temporarily because it’s the only way he can afford to support Carly and the baby. She doesn’t plan to love Hank, after all it’s only a marriage of convenience, but soon enough she’s madly in love with him. Hank’s loved her all along. She doesn’t want to burden him with a blind wife but Hank won’t live without her. He’ll do anything to keep her with him. <br /><br />Wow, these cowboys they just don’t take no for an answer. Once they have their minds set there is no changing it. Love it! Hank was so patient with Carly and he knew he had to make things right with her. I really liked the part when Hank apologized with the flashcards. It was so cute and very unique! Hank wasn’t the richest man and he was willing to give up everything for Carly. He’d rather be in debt than live without her. I really love this series and can’t wait to read the rest! <br /></span>

<div id="review_107651022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107651022" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/667272-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376230788p2/667272.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107651022?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/667272-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/667272-christine?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107651022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1400061079216981246">Absolutely fabulous love story...human, beautiful, tragic, and perfect!<br/><br/>Full disclosure: I am legally blind, a far cry from the blackness that our heroine, Carly, has had to deal with her entire life, but it does make me feel drawn toward blind and visually disabled characters. On the other hand, I am also very, very picky about how those characters are portrayed. So often, I feel like perhaps the author put a blindfold on and tried to walk around for a few hours, without really getting to know w</span>
  <span id="freeText1400061079216981246" style="display:none">Absolutely fabulous love story...human, beautiful, tragic, and perfect!<br /><br />Full disclosure: I am legally blind, a far cry from the blackness that our heroine, Carly, has had to deal with her entire life, but it does make me feel drawn toward blind and visually disabled characters. On the other hand, I am also very, very picky about how those characters are portrayed. So often, I feel like perhaps the author put a blindfold on and tried to walk around for a few hours, without really getting to know what it is like to be blind or visually disabled. In this case, however; I was completely drawn in to the heart, mind, and gradually blurring world of Carly Adams. At one point, as her waning visual acuity slipped to a level approximately akin to my own, I felt like someone had borrowed my own eyes for a short time and even, though I'm a little chagrined to admit it, my own psyche, because Carly pretended to see things she couldn't to spare other's feelings (and her own pride) -- something I have done.<br /><br />But enough about that, on to the story! The setup is this: Carly has been blind her entire life and a week before the novel begins, a surgery gives her the ability to see for the first time. Everything is new and she has to train her eyes like a newborn -- learning colors, letters, numbers, and making sense out of rapid motion. She and her friend go to a bar to celebrate and to give Carly a chance to watch people dance, but she runs into a rather extraordinarily drunk Hank Coulter there and falls for his lines. Their resulting encounter leaves her pregnant, which, given her recent surgery, is a very bad thing.<br /><br />This wasn't an easy romance. There were real obstacles to overcome and real challenges to surmount, and I can't count the number of times my heart gave a little twang of desperate sympathy. Technically, there are a few things I could nit pick, but I don't really want to.<br /><br />I absolutely recommend this book to anyone. Yes, it's a romance novel, but even if you are only occasionally drawn to love stories, you will probably enjoy this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1400061079216981246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2115177450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2115177450" />
    <a title="Bookishbreeze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55634595-bookishbreeze"><img alt="Bookishbreeze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471748637p2/55634595.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2115177450?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookishbreeze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookishbreeze" href="/user/show/55634595-bookishbreeze">Bookishbreeze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55634595-bookishbreeze?shelf=contemp-rom">contemp-rom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55634595-bookishbreeze?shelf=do-not-read">do-not-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2115177450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16545477639527800971">This book is bad, even for the shallow HR in disguise I was expecting (and even looking forward to). But the biggest, headliner reason why I think so seems to differ wildly from most others. In short: the H is a complete piece of crap, at least before I reached my limit and stopped.<br/><br/>Most people's reviews that I've read so far have complained about the heroine in this book, and I couldn't possibly say for myself if she was intolerable or not. She was just naive as hell and dumb from what I read, b</span>
  <span id="freeText16545477639527800971" style="display:none">This book is bad, even for the shallow HR in disguise I was expecting (and even looking forward to). But the biggest, headliner reason why I think so seems to differ wildly from most others. In short: the H is a complete piece of crap, at least before I reached my limit and stopped.<br /><br />Most people's reviews that I've read so far have complained about the heroine in this book, and I couldn't possibly say for myself if she was intolerable or not. She was just naive as hell and dumb from what I read, but I DNF'd about five minutes after Hank wakes up after the one night stand. <br /><br />What I don't understand about these reviews I'm seeing, however, is why no one seems to have a problem with Hank's behavior! I even see people saying he did nothing wrong. Maybe he redeems himself later on; and, from what I can tell, Carly does become fairly insufferable by contrast. But did everyone conveniently forget how he acts when they meet? I'm honestly confused here. He treats sexually active women like used fleshlights, flip-flops so hard on Carly's place in the whore/Madonna complex that I practically got whiplash, and his actions toward her in the end may or may not have constituted rape. Let me show you some direct quotes from this book from this scumbag.<br /><br /><b>First, in regards to the oh-so-flattering way he treats the women who, JUST LIKE HIM, choose to exercise their right to have sex for the sake of sex:</b><br /> <blockquote>Aside from telling a woman he loved her, he’d say almost anything to score</blockquote><br />(already charming, this one, but he goes on to say)<br /><blockquote>The gals who frequented places like Chaps normally came for the same reasons men did and understood the unspoken rules...It was fun, meaningless, and in the morning, no one looked back. Hank liked it that way. He wasn’t ready to get locked down. If he had been, he sure as hell wouldn’t shop for a wife in a bar where all the prospects had been ridden hard and put away wet by countless other men</blockquote><br />-So let me get this straight. Despite the fact that Hank a)likes one night stands, b)considers them harmless, and c) seemingly understands that women can have the same wants, he still IMMEDIATELY, in the same goddamn paragraph, says these women aren't good enough for him. Because he's such a catch, apparently.<br /><br /><b>Now I'd like to transition to the way he discusses Carly:</b><br /><blockquote>"Hank tried to decide what it was about her that he found so appealing. He’d met a lot of gorgeous women in bars and never wanted any of them the way he wanted her. Maybe it was her sweet face...What an illusion. No woman her age was still innocent, and if, by some weird chance, she were, she sure as hell wouldn’t be hanging out in a place like Chaps.</blockquote><br />-so, here we establish that even though he himself thinks she looks innocent, he immediately writes her off as a whore...for being in a bar that <b>he already knows she's never been in before.</b> Am I supposed to take from this that all women who go to bars are sluts looking for some? Because Carly herself already explains earlier in the story that she's just there for her friend, and he notes that she's clearly not from around there <b>multiple times and in different ways</b>, which she confirms, so this assumption cannot possibly be based just on this one bar's reputation.<br /><br /><blockquote>At the back of his mind, alarm bells clanged even as he ran a hand inside her jeans to touch her moist, hot center. Then he thought, “What can it hurt?” Women who hung out in bars usually took the Pill. Barring an unwanted pregnancy, wherein lay the risk? She was too damned sweet to be carrying an STD, and he knew damned well that he wasn’t.</blockquote><br />-so even drunk he knows damn well that he should be putting on a condom, first of all. Secondly, he just called her a slut a couple pages ago by alluding to the face that she can't possibly be different from other women at the bar, who we already established he thinks are used goods and then some. So why is she now "too sweet" to have an STI if she's just like them? And you don't have to be un-sweet to catch those anyway, jackass. All it takes is one cheating ex. Also, way to go assuming she must be taking the pill. Real smart. She's apparently slutty enough for the pill (since she is a Bar Woman™) but somehow not slutty enough for STIs?<br /><br />Finally, the pièce de résistance, the day after the fact:<br /><blockquote>It wasn’t Charlie’s fault that she was pretty, and as much as he might like to shift the blame, he couldn’t hold her accountable for his own behavior. When he’d ordered her the slammer, his sole intent had been to get her drunk. She’d been staggering by the time they left Chaps, and he’d taken full advantage of it.</blockquote><br />-Folks, <b>he admits that he purposefully got her so drunk that she couldn't walk straight, explicitly to have sex with her. </b> The <i>only</i> reason I'm not outright calling this sexual assault is because he was supposedly also drunk. HOWEVER, he was thinking clearly enough to plot to get her drunk in the first place, while he got her so drunk she could barely walk on her own, apparently. So even if we don't call it rape, how could anyone call him blameless in the debacle when he deliberately takes advantage of a drunk women that he himself ensured would be too smashed for clear thought? How are people not calling him out on this? It's right there in black and white on the page!<br /><br />As a counterpoint, never let it be said that I find Carly completely blameless in all this. She drank hard liquor that she was <i>warned</i> would be strong, even after her doctor told her to be careful with alcohol on account of her meds. She didn't insist on a condom when they did have sex, though I'm not entirely sure she was "with it" enough to understand what was happening until too late, since she seemed a tad too quiet and confused during the scene.<br /> <br />Tellingly, this exchange occurs before the event:<br /><blockquote>“Good. My aim is to loosen you up, not knock you on your butt.” She eyed him over the rim of the glass. <br />“Trying to ply me with liquor?”<br />“Damn straight.”</blockquote><br />While Hank is clearly lying about how drunk he wants her, based on his admission the day after, he is outright admitting his intent. Yeah, it's clearly meant to be taken as a joke, but like my mom always says, when someone tells you who they are, believe them.<br /><br />Nevertheless, I'm kind of flabbergasted at what really feels like a lot of victim-blaming in these reviews. So many I've seen outright say it was all her fault, when the book is courteous enough to explicitly state that the H deliberately impaired her judgement and then took advantage. Someone said that it takes two to tango, and considering how dumb Carly was with her own safety, I'm tempted to agree with that sentiment, but even then it isn't "all her fault." Even scummy Hank, with all his dubious morals in the beginning, knows better than to foist all the blame on her.<br /><br />Still, This book is terrible regardless. I couldn't sit through it. It was just really, really ill thought out, and everyone criticizing it seems to at least be on the same page about that.<br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16545477639527800971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer3220172411955867415">In the beginning of the book, I thought Hank Coulter was the most irresponsible, annoying, selfish, and thought-less person ever. I truly hated him. However, as the book progressed, we see what a sweet, nice person he could be.<br/><br/>There were multiple times during the book that his words and actions towards Carly was so sweet and emotional that I could not hold back tears. Still, he was a too forceful a guy. I HATED that about him!!! <br/><br/>Carly is a sweet and nice person who has eye disease. As a result, </span>
  <span id="freeText3220172411955867415" style="display:none">In the beginning of the book, I thought Hank Coulter was the most irresponsible, annoying, selfish, and thought-less person ever. I truly hated him. However, as the book progressed, we see what a sweet, nice person he could be.<br /><br />There were multiple times during the book that his words and actions towards Carly was so sweet and emotional that I could not hold back tears. Still, he was a too forceful a guy. I HATED that about him!!! <br /><br />Carly is a sweet and nice person who has eye disease. As a result, she has been blind for the first 28 years of her life. She gains eyesight after a surgery, but after a one-night stand with Hank, she becomes pregnant and starts to lose her eyesight until she becomes completely blind. Hank tries his best to help her with her fading eyesight (e.g. takes her on a trip to see things she always wanted to see, like zoo animals, lets her drive because she has always wanted to do that, etc.). However, he messes up at times. I was upset about that but the fact that he was not always a perfect guy who never makes any mistakes made this book realistic.<br /><br />So far, it seems as if in most of the books of this series, the heroine has some sort of either physical or mental disability. I wish Catherine Anderson would write a book where the hero has a disability. It would be an interesting read. <br />I have read multiple books by her wherein the heroine has a disability and the hero is considerate and totally in love with her. It would be a nice change to read a book where the position are reversed, i.e. the hero has a disability.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer18318937" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6376636287545329260">Anderson's books are pure romance and drama, and always very poignant. She tells people-stories, and Blue Skies is no different. She really draws you in with her multi-faceted characters, all the angst, and emotions. These types of stories generally aren't my favorites, but I have enjoyed Anderson's books.<br/><br/>Hank and Carly had an instant chemistry. Their story definitely keeps you reading. It was interesting to read how the characters changed and grew, learned from their mistakes, and tried to buil</span>
  <span id="freeText6376636287545329260" style="display:none">Anderson's books are pure romance and drama, and always very poignant. She tells people-stories, and Blue Skies is no different. She really draws you in with her multi-faceted characters, all the angst, and emotions. These types of stories generally aren't my favorites, but I have enjoyed Anderson's books.<br /><br />Hank and Carly had an instant chemistry. Their story definitely keeps you reading. It was interesting to read how the characters changed and grew, learned from their mistakes, and tried to build a trust between them. Carly's struggle with her eyesight adds a whole other dimension to the story that makes the book a great read. You end up really feeling for the characters. At times in the beginning Carly kind of pisses me off because she is a bit unfair to Hank, but you kind of understand where she is coming from.<br /><br />I enjoyed reading the book. It's a great love story that goes through trials and tribulations that are a bit atypical of other romances. If you want to read a poignant romance, then I definitely recommend this book.</span>

Although his actions weren’t ideal, I understood him a little better than Carly which is why I found her so frustrating. <div id="review_24673454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24673454" />
    <a title="Julianna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/883725-julianna"><img alt="Julianna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442976820p2/883725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24673454?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna" href="/user/show/883725-julianna">Julianna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Disabled Heroines, Beta Heroes, Contemporary Romance</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=desert-island-keepers">desert-island-keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24673454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18111868740229402673">Reviewed for <a href='http://www.thcreviews.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>THC Reviews</a><br/>"4.5 stars" <i>Blue Skies</i> is another tender, emotional romance from Catherine Anderson's pen. In the tradition of <i>Phantom Waltz</i>, an earlier book from the same series, Ms. Anderson has created a disabled heroine, one who is this time blind. I was very impressed when I found out through the author's note at the end of the book that <i>Blue Skies</i> was inspired by a real-life young woman who had contacted her following the release of <i>Phantom Waltz</i>. This lady suffered from the same r</span>
  <span id="freeText18111868740229402673" style="display:none">Reviewed for <a href="http://www.thcreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">THC Reviews</a><br />"4.5 stars" <i>Blue Skies</i> is another tender, emotional romance from Catherine Anderson's pen. In the tradition of <i>Phantom Waltz</i>, an earlier book from the same series, Ms. Anderson has created a disabled heroine, one who is this time blind. I was very impressed when I found out through the author's note at the end of the book that <i>Blue Skies</i> was inspired by a real-life young woman who had contacted her following the release of <i>Phantom Waltz</i>. This lady suffered from the same rare eye disease that Carly does and Ms. Anderson consulted with her and her doctor to make sure she got all the medical details correct. I think the research showed, and as a result, Blue Skies was a very touching, inspiring story that has become one of my favorites from this author.<br /><br />Carly Adams was born blind, but through surgery was able to regain her sight just one week before the novel begins. She is a tough woman who has learned to live independently in spite of her disability. Carly goes to a bar with her best friend where she sits admiring Hank Coulter from afar. She can hardly believe it when the handsome cowboy approaches her and invites her to dance, then spends the rest of the evening sweet-talking her. Later, when Hank takes her out to his truck for a little hanky-panky, things don't go well in more ways than one, and she ends up pregnant. My only real issue with this book is that Carly was a little too stubborn at times. Not only was she contrary, but she was also somewhat contradictory too, making me occasionally want to leap into the story to shake some sense into her. Carly was understandably upset about what happened between her and Hank, and especially about the fact that she was now pregnant as a result. I did understand that she felt Hank had treated her callously and that she now had to face the possibility of loosing her sight again after having just regained it, so on some level, her continuously turning Hank away made sense. However, if I were in her shoes, I think I would have been so concerned about financial matters and what might happen without his help that I'd at least have been willing to listen to him. Carly is also pretty stand-offish with Hank even after they get married. I realize that their first time together was pretty crappy, and she believes that Hank was only looking to get laid which is pretty much the truth. However, from the moment Hank realized what he had done, he was absolutely nothing but nice to her, simply wanting to take care of her and their baby, yet she jumps at his slightest touch almost like a woman who's been raped. Thankfully, Carly does slowly come around and starts to consider the fact that she was as turned on by him as he was by her and from there things become really sweet and romantic as well as a little steamy. But when she left him again, I was starting to get rather frustrated with her. She also doesn't communicate well with Hank sometimes. Knowledge of her condition and things that happened in the past that still affect her today had to come from her friend and her father, a plot device which I'm usually not fond of. It didn't bother me quite as much as it has in some other romances, but I still would have liked to see a little more vulnerability from her in that respect. I hope I don't sound too critical of Carly though, because ultimately, she was a sweet young woman who was also an inspirational character in many ways for her positive can-do attitude and for not allowing the blindness to get the best of her.<br /><br />Hank was an absolutely dreamy hero. In the opening chapter, he is a real seductive charmer in spite of being under the influence of alcohol. If I had been Carly, I don't think I could have resisted him either. Of course, he was totally off him game when it came their first sexual encounter which left him with a whole lot to make up for, but he ended up doing an incredible job of it. I love that he was a man who took his responsibilities seriously. He immediately started trying to find Carly the minute his foggy memories began to resurface. When he found out she was pregnant, he repeatedly offered her financial and moral support even though she kept blowing him off and refusing to talk to him. I like that he could get tough and put his foot down when he needed to. He could be equally as tenacious as Carly could be although in a good way instead of a frustratingly obstinate way, but overall he was a sweet beta hero who was willing to move heaven and earth to be with Carly once he realized he was in love with her. I love how Hank tenderly cared for Carly when she was sick on their wedding night, as well as all the concessions he made and things he did for her both before and after they were married. The way he completely renovated his ranch to accommodate Carly's disability reminded me of Ryan from <i>Phantom Waltz</i>, another of my favorite Catherine Anderson heroes. Hank trying to show Carly all the things he possibly could in order to make wonderful memories before she lost her sight again was also very romantic. Hank was just a thoughtful, patient, kindhearted and thoroughly loving man who has definitely earned a spot on my all-time favorite heroes list.<br /><br />Hank and Carly are certainly the stars of the “show.” There are a few secondary characters, but mostly they play relatively small roles. Hank's sister, Bethany and her husband, Ryan (<i>Phantom Waltz</i>), as well as Hank's brother Jake and his wife, Molly (<i>Sweet Nothings</i>) were there to support Hank and Carly. Rafe and Maggie (<i>Baby Love</i>) appear at a couple of family gatherings, but don't have any actual lines. Another of Hank's brothers, Zeke, gets a pretty good introduction as the calm voice of reason when Hank needs a shoulder to lean on. Zeke gets to be the hero of the next book in the series, <i>Bright Eyes</i>. <br /><br />In spite of Carly's stubbornness, <i>Blue Skies</i> turned out to be a wonderful read. I can't imagine what it must be like to loose one's sight, but Catherine Anderson gives the reader a seemingly authentic look into the life of a blind woman. Not only that, but she also created a story that was deeply emotional and sweetly romantic with a hero to die for. I couldn't have asked for much more. <i>Blue Skies</i> is the fourth book in Ms. Anderson's <i>Kendrick/Coulter/Harrigan Families</i> series. It has earned a spot on my keeper shelf and I look forward to reading more from this series soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18111868740229402673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11390998693197440642">Catherine Anderson delivers an absolutely beautiful love story in Blue Skies. The details into the eye disease that the main character, Carly Adams, has and the fact that Anderson wrote this book after a fan that wrote a letter warmed my heart. I have MS and I wish more authors would write stories with characters having chronic illnesses and diseases. <br/><br/>Carly Adams is 28 years old and has only had her eye sight restored for a few weeks when she goes out to a honky tonk with her best friend, her ro</span>
  <span id="freeText11390998693197440642" style="display:none">Catherine Anderson delivers an absolutely beautiful love story in Blue Skies. The details into the eye disease that the main character, Carly Adams, has and the fact that Anderson wrote this book after a fan that wrote a letter warmed my heart. I have MS and I wish more authors would write stories with characters having chronic illnesses and diseases. <br /><br />Carly Adams is 28 years old and has only had her eye sight restored for a few weeks when she goes out to a honky tonk with her best friend, her roommate, Bess. Can you imagine spending the majority of your life without eyesight and having it restored. Never having seen so many things before Carly only plans on observing the dancers and patrons at the bar. This is definitely a live changing night for her in so many ways.<br /><br />Hank Coulter, spots Carly across the bar when he's dancing. He sets his sights on making Carly the woman he spends the evening with. He only remembers bits and pieces from the evening after waking up in the back floorboard of his truck in the bar parking lot. <br /><br />I'm not going to go into the plot further just know this is an incredible love story and gives outstanding insight into what a blind person goes through on a daily basis and into what it would be like when their sight is restored. A must read.</span>

  <span id="freeText901947873094587817" style="display:none">In this lovely romance I learned a little about lattice dystrophy, a rare condition of the eyes which can cause blindness. Although I googled it I didn't find a lot.<br /><br />Carly Adams was born blind with both lattice dystrophy and cataracts. Although surgery gave her sight, it would not last forever. The insight which this story gave me into the world of the blind was both heartwarming and heartbreaking. Not only how a blind person experiences the world but how difficult it is for a sighted person to comprehend. Fortunately, Carly finds true love and happiness with a handsome cowboy and lives happily ever after (did I mention this was a romance?) in spite of her handicap. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2100462875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2100462875" />
    <a title="Monika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11985185-monika"><img alt="Monika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502036860p2/11985185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2100462875?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monika" href="/user/show/11985185-monika">Monika</a>

        rated it

<div id="review_1028626008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1028626008" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13012187-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348185636p2/13012187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1028626008?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/13012187-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13012187-sara?shelf=a-real-eye-roller">a-real-eye-roller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13012187-sara?shelf=decent-second-act">decent-second-act</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028626008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17041172290777018277">I didn't expect much from this book when I read the back cover, so at least I wasn't disappointed. Carly Adams just had surgery to correct a lifetime of blindness, enjoys a night at the bar with her friend Bess and winds up being deflowered by Hank Coulter. Without a condom.<br/><br/>Surprise surprise, she gets knocked up and the pregnancy will fuck up her eyes again. The whole situation is teeth-gratingly annoying to read through. Carly's a stubborn ass who whines about her stupid pride, Hank's just an a</span>
  <span id="freeText17041172290777018277" style="display:none">I didn't expect much from this book when I read the back cover, so at least I wasn't disappointed. Carly Adams just had surgery to correct a lifetime of blindness, enjoys a night at the bar with her friend Bess and winds up being deflowered by Hank Coulter. Without a condom.<br /><br />Surprise surprise, she gets knocked up and the pregnancy will fuck up her eyes again. The whole situation is teeth-gratingly annoying to read through. Carly's a stubborn ass who whines about her stupid pride, Hank's just an ass period, we have yet another stupid "marry me or else" blackmail plot and the original "do it or I'll take your baby away" stipulation, Bess tries to be a good friend but ends up temporarily on Carly's shitlist when she's forced to convince Hank to bully Carly into marriage because Carly won't stop being a stubborn ass and it's just really, really annoying.<br /><br />That said, this isn't Anderson's worst book. It's not her best by a long shot and the romance is nothing to write home about, but it has its good moments here and there. After their impromptu wedding, Hank and Carly get to know each other and he nurses her through her terrible morning sickness. We get a cameo from Sunset, the horse from Jake's book. And Zeke catching the bouquet at the wedding got a laugh out of me, I admit it. Of all the ways to go "hey, guess who's getting married next book!" this was the most creative.<br /><br />Most of the second half of the book isn't too bad, either. Hank and Carly build a friendship, Carly spends her time going <i>I can't love him I won't love him</i> but of course she does, and he loves her, and during a vacation to Portland they finally have satisfying sex. Meanwhile, Carly's eyesight is going and going and she tries not to let it depress her until one day she nearly drowns in a pond. She's rushed to the hospital, totally freaks out and goes home to her dad. Of course. It's not an Anderson book without the heroine running away from the man!<br /><br />And it turns out Carly has a skeleton in her closet named Michael, an old boyfriend who dumped her when she wouldn't put out, left her alone in the woods and she almost drowned back then, too! The story lierally infodumps this on us at the last stretch, we're given next to no foreshadowing aside from the almost-drowning scene and Art Adams telling Hank happened offscreen. I was just kind of like "lol wut" at the whole thing.<br /><br />But of course, Carly and Hank are meant to be together and stay that way, Carly has the kid and Hank describes how he looks and the morning light, the end.<br /><br />So yes. I liked about 80% of the second half of the book and the standard sweet ending well enough, but everything else was trite and predictable and annoying.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17041172290777018277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97889828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97889828" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1951999-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484586527p2/1951999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97889828?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/1951999-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97889828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12498039748269792775">The heroines of this series often have interesting and unusual histories (paralysis, brain damage, domestic violence, agoraphobia), and this one is no exception. Carley has lattice dystrophy, a childhood blindness that she just had surgery for, and she can see for the first time. Then she gets pregnant, which causes the disease to return with a vengeance. <br/><br/>This story just has too many out-of-character moments to be among Anderson's best. Carley's life-long best friend takes her to a skanky cowboy</span>
  <span id="freeText12498039748269792775" style="display:none">The heroines of this series often have interesting and unusual histories (paralysis, brain damage, domestic violence, agoraphobia), and this one is no exception. Carley has lattice dystrophy, a childhood blindness that she just had surgery for, and she can see for the first time. Then she gets pregnant, which causes the disease to return with a vengeance. <br /><br />This story just has too many out-of-character moments to be among Anderson's best. Carley's life-long best friend takes her to a skanky cowboy bar three weeks after she regains her sight, then leaves her for long stretches. Nah. Carley has spent her entire life taking on the world and finding ways to make life work for her and on her terms, then blames the entire scenario (till late in the book) on Hank. Nah. She takes charge of nearly everything -- her life, her activities, her schooling -- then passively feels manipulated into marrying Hank for the finances and health coverage. Why didn't she demand those of him and why wasn't she the one to set the terms? It just doesn't hold together as well as other storylines.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12498039748269792775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VIB95p+Ykev3QNQ9xkI7Me4c1h7Sq4WU7lPZV5by7vxo4hieNndvBfkyGg2w3GZa/wLRW7QB64mFMXjTy6UKiA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sTq8VU2sfa7mP8ndg8TGLNE/Sd0gJJeehjjySok4p1yNWNkt5EODQOhNB+31WptHwCFOmEaO+YPtWlPO1G9DKA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer4389155454562057887"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br/>(1)romance author:<br/>Adeline Catherine was born and raised in Grants Pass, Oregon, USA. She always yearned to be a writer like her mother. The morning that one of her professors asked if she could use samples of Catherine’s creative writing on an overhead projector to teach was</span>
  <span id="freeText4389155454562057887" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br />(1)romance author:<br />Adeline Catherine was born and raised in Grants Pass, Oregon, USA. She always yearned to be a writer like her mother. The morning that one of her professors asked if she could use samples of Catherine’s creative writing on an overhead projector to teach was a dream come true. In 1988, she sold her first book to Harlequin Intrigue and went on to write three more before she tried her hand at a single-title historical romance. Nine books later, she did her first single-title contemporary.<br /><br />Catherine married Sidney D. Anderson, an industrial electrician and entrepreneur. They had two sons, Sidney D. Jr. and John G. In 2001 she and her husband purchased a central Oregon home located on a ridge with incredible mountain views and surrounded by forestland honeycombed with trails. It was her dream home, a wonderland in the winter and beyond beautiful in the summer. She named it Cinnamon Ridge after the huge ponderosa pines on the property, which sport bark the color of cinnamon.<br /><br />Sadly, Catherine lost her husband to a long-term illness in 2014. She has kept Cinnamon Ridge as her primary residence but divides her time between there and her son John's farm, where she has the support of her loved ones and can enjoy his horses, cows, and raise her own chickens.<br /><br />Catherine loves animals and birds, both wild and domestic. She presently has two Australian shepherds, six cats, and a very old canary. She is very family oriented as well. Her older son has lived in Japan, Australia, and now resides in New Zealand. Catherine and her stateside family will celebrate Christmas on the north island with Sidney, his wife Mary, and their two sons, Liam and Jonas.</span>

Only Quincy, she says, as the sole remaining Harrigan bachelor, can make it happen—by marrying Ceara. To Quincy, Ceara is a charming and quite likely deranged spinner of dreams who can’t prove she’s telling the truth. But how can he pass up any attempt to restore Loni to health?       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1333326-blue-skies">Quotes from Blue Skies</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;That my eyes are yours as well. When you go blind, I’ll draw pictures with words so you can still see all the beautiful things. You told me once that the most gorgeous thing you first saw was the Central Oregon blue sky. That’s my vow to you, Carly—nothing but blue skies for the rest of our lives, even after you go permanently blind.”<br />.<br />He bent at the knees to catch her up in his arms. As he carried her toward the cabin, she gazed up at his beautiful face, drinking in every hard line and chiseled plane so she could remember it later. If she were given a choice of one thing she could remember and take with her into total grayness, it wouldn’t be a sunset or a gorgeous blue sky.<br /><br />It would be her memory of the love she saw shining in Hank Coulter’s eyes.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/9631776-that-my-eyes-are-yours-as-well-when-you-go">0 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;With Hank at her side, she would never really be blind again. His eyes were hers, just as he’d vowed. When they grew old, they would take walks at sunset, and she’d be able to see everything. His gift to her—pictures painted with words. Love wasn’t about easy, according to Hank. It was about sticking through thick and thin. He would always be with her, unless death took him first, and even then, Carly knew she’d never be left in complete darkness again.<br /><br />She would have the love of this man to light her way.&rdquo;</span>
